## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most commonly appear in constitutive laws for elasticity/plasticity and thermoelasticity. Temperature typically enters through thermal expansion (stress depends on mechanical strain minus thermal strain) and through temperature-dependent stiffness/flow stress (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (1D linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain linear elastic response; c0 is Young’s modulus)
- Linear thermoelasticity with thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential in T): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (stronger/weaker stiffness with temperature over a range)
- Nonlinear elastic (Landau-type polynomial): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (strain stiffening/softening beyond linear regime)
- Nonlinear thermoelastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (plastic/flow-like scaling with strain; temperature alters strength factor)
- Saturating (smooth yield/transition) stress–strain: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) (initially linear, then approaches a plateau/saturation stress)
- Thermally softened saturation: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (plateau level changes systematically with temperature)
- Neo-Hookean-like 1D hyperelastic (using stretch 1+epsilon): sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - c1 / (1 + epsilon)**2) (finite-strain elasticity; nonlinear at larger strains)
- Rational stiffness degradation with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + T) (effective modulus decreases with increasing T)
- Smooth elastic–plastic blend (tanh switch): sigma = (c0 * epsilon) * (1 - tanh(c1 * (epsilon - c2))) + (c3 + c4 * (epsilon - c2)**c5) * tanh(c1 * (epsilon - c2)) (elastic at small strain, hardening beyond a yield-like strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear elasticity → sigma proportional to epsilon (straight-line region; slope is an effective modulus).
- Thermal expansion under constraint → sigma depends on (epsilon minus a term proportional to T - reference), capturing stress-free thermal strain.
- Thermal softening/hardening → multiplicative temperature factor on stress scale, e.g., exp(c*T) or (c0 + c1*T), rather than adding T alone.
- Strain stiffening/softening → odd-power nonlinearities in epsilon (e.g., epsilon**3) that preserve sign of sigma with sign of epsilon.
- Yield-like transition without explicit piecewise rules → tanh(c*(epsilon-c)) or similar smooth switches blending elastic and plastic branches.
- Plateau/locking behavior at large strain → tanh(c*epsilon) or rational forms that approach a finite asymptote as |epsilon| grows.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical interaction → cross terms like epsilon*T indicating that temperature changes the sensitivity of stress to strain.
- Finite-strain effects → dependence on (1+epsilon) and inverse powers (e.g., 1/(1+epsilon)**2), indicating stretch-based hyperelastic structure.

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci14)
============================================================
GT: -c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)
Candidates evaluated: 68
Matched candidate IDs: [36, 68]
Matched candidates: ["T*c0 + T*c1*Abs(epsilon)**c2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7 + c8*Abs(epsilon)**c2", "T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon**c7*Abs(T)"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$-c_0(T - c_1) + \epsilon^{c_2} \cdot c_3 \cdot (T - c_4)$$

With c1 = c4 = 352.1579..., so:
$$(-c_0 + c_3 \epsilon^{c_2})(T - c_1)$$

Expanding:
$$-c_0 T + c_0 c_1 + c_3 \epsilon^{c_2} T - c_3 c_1 \epsilon^{c_2}$$

So the GT has the form:
$$T(-c_0 + c_3 \epsilon^{c_2}) + c_0 c_1 - c_3 c_1 \epsilon^{c_2}$$

This can be written as:
$$T \cdot A + T \cdot B \cdot \epsilon^{c_2} + C + D \cdot \epsilon^{c_2}$$

where A = -c_0, B = c_3, C = c_0·c_1, D = -c_3·c_1.

Key structural features:
- Linear in T
- Contains T·ε^{c2} (a product of T and a fractional power of epsilon)
- Contains a constant term
- Contains ε^{c2} term
- No pure linear epsilon term (unless c2=1, but c2≈0.626)

The basis functions are: {1, T, ε^{c2}, T·ε^{c2}}

Now let me check each candidate. For a match, the candidate must be able to produce exactly these four basis functions (and zero out everything else).

**Key constraint:** The GT requires a **T·ε^{c2}** cross-term. This is critical.

Let me systematically check which candidates can produce this term.

### Candidates without T·ε^{power} cross-term:

Many candidates have terms like `T*c0` and `epsilon**c2` separately but no `T*epsilon**c` cross-term. These cannot match because T·ε^{c2} is linearly independent from T and ε^{c2} separately.

Let me identify candidates that have T·ε^{power} cross-terms or equivalent:

- **Candidate 10**: T*c0*epsilon + ... (T·epsilon, not T·ε^{c2})
- **Candidate 11**: T*c0*epsilon + ... (same issue)
- **Candidate 26**: T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + ... (T·epsilon, not T·ε^{c2})
- **Candidate 27**: T*c1*epsilon + ... (same)
- **Candidate 31**: T*c1*epsilon + ... + c5*epsilon**c6*exp(T*c7) (T·epsilon plus exponential)
- **Candidate 33**: T*c1*epsilon + ... 
- **Candidate 36**: T*c1*|ε|^{c2} + ... (This has T·|ε|^{c2} which under ε≥0 is T·ε^{c2}!)
- **Candidate 49**: T*c0*epsilon + ... (T·epsilon)
- **Candidate 51**: T*c0*epsilon + ...
- **Candidate 65**: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + ... (This has T·ε^{c1}!)
- **Candidate 66**: T*c0*epsilon**c1 + ... (This has T·ε^{c1}!)
- **Candidate 67**: ... + c4*epsilon**c5*|T| (ε^{c5}·|T| which under T≥0 is T·ε^{c5})
- **Candidate 68**: ... + c6*epsilon**c7*|T| (same idea)

Also candidates with exp(T·c) terms could potentially... no, exponentials can't match linear T dependence.

Candidates with `c·epsilon**c·(T+c)**c` type terms:
- **Candidate 50**: c6*epsilon*(T+c7)**c8 - if c8=1, this gives c6*epsilon*(T+c7) = c6*epsilon*T + c6*c7*epsilon. But this is T·epsilon, not T·ε^{c2}.

Let me now carefully analyze the promising candidates.

### Candidate 36:
`T*c0 + T*c1*|epsilon|^{c2} + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7 + c8*|epsilon|^{c2}`

Under ε ≥ 0, |ε| = ε:
= T*c0 + T*c1*ε^{c2} + c3*ε^{c4} + c5*ε + c6*ε^{c7} + c8*ε^{c2}

GT needs: T·A + T·B·ε^{c2} + C + D·ε^{c2}

Setting c4, c5, c6, c7 to eliminate unwanted terms: set c5=0 (kills linear ε), and we need c3*ε^{c4} + c6*ε^{c7} to contribute a constant C. Set c4=0: c3*ε^0 = c3 (constant). Set c6=0 to kill ε^{c7}.

So: T*c0 + T*c1*ε^{c2} + c3 + c8*ε^{c2}

This matches! {T, T·ε^{c2}, 1, ε^{c2}} ✓

Candidate 36 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 65:
`T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*log(c5*exp(T*c6 + c7*epsilon) + 1) + c8*epsilon**c1`

The log term is problematic. Setting c4=0 eliminates it:
= T*c0*ε^{c1} + c2*ε^{c3} + c8*ε^{c1}

This gives {T·ε^{c1}, ε^{c3}, ε^{c1}} but no constant and no pure T term. Missing basis functions.

Can't set c4≠0 without introducing non-linear T dependence. 

Candidate 65 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 66:
`T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon + c3*log(c4*exp(T*c5 + c6*epsilon) + 1) + c7*epsilon**c1`

Setting c3=0: T*c0*ε^{c1} + c2*ε + c7*ε^{c1}
Missing constant and pure T terms.

Candidate 66 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 67:
`T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5*|T|`

Under T ≥ 0, |T| = T:
= T*c0 + c1*ε + c2*ε^{c3} + c4*T*ε^{c5}

This gives {T, ε, ε^{c3}, T·ε^{c5}}. 

GT needs {T, T·ε^{c2}, 1, ε^{c2}}. Set c1=0 (kill ε), set c3=0 so c2*ε^0 = c2 (constant), c5 = GT's c2.

= T*c0 + c2 + c4*T*ε^{c5}

This gives {T, 1, T·ε^{c5}} but missing ε^{c2} term. Not enough terms.

Candidate 67 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 68:
`T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon**c7*|T|`

Under T ≥ 0:
= T*c0 + c1*ε^{c2} + c3*ε + c4*ε^{c5} + c6*T*ε^{c7}

Set c3=0, and set one of c4*ε^{c5} to be a constant by c5=0: c4 = constant.
Then: T*c0 + c1*ε^{c2} + c4 + c6*T*ε^{c7}

Basis: {T, ε^{c2}, 1, T·ε^{c7}} with c2=c7 → matches GT! ✓

Candidate 68 verdict: [MATCH]

Candidates 30,37,38,46: Have ε^{c}·exp(T·c) which isn't T·ε^{c}.
Candidates 10,11,49,51: Have T·ε (linear product).

For candidates 1-9, 12-25, 28-29, 32, 34-35, 37-48, 50, 52-64: None have T·ε^{power} cross-terms, so they cannot match.
